Then write a predicate `optimal` that holds on an expression if it has no additions by 0. Then write an optimizer `optimize` that removes all additions by 0. Then write a lemma `OptimizerOptimal` that ensures `optimal(optimize(e))` for all expressions `e`.
### Hint: This is the definiton of the `optimal` predicate:
predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}
### Hint: Don't use the same structure for `optimize` as for `optimal`. Instead, follow the next hint.
### Hint: In the addition case, the `optimize` function should recursively optimize the sub-expressions and then match on the optimized sub-expressions.
### Hint: Do NOT use `requires` anywhere.
### Hint: Write the lemma as
lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))

match e

case _ => 3
### Hint: For the proof, just do a simple pattern match (match not if) and call the lemma recursively without adding asserts.

```dafny
datatype Expr =
  | Const(i: int)
  | Var(name: string)
  | Add(e1: Expr, e2: Expr)

predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}

function optimize(e: Expr): Expr
{
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e2);
    if e1_opt == Const(0) then e2_opt
    else if e2_opt == Const(0) then e1_opt
    else Add(e1_opt, e2_opt)

   |

   |                             ^

```dafny
datatype Expr =
  | Const(i: int)
  | Var(name: string)
  | Add(e1: Expr, e2: Expr)

predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}

function optimize(e: Expr): Expr
{
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e2);
    if e1_opt == Const(0) then e2_opt
    else if e2_opt == Const(0) then e1_opt
    else Add(e1_opt, e2_opt)
  case _ => e
}

  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
{

  }

    var e2 := e.e2;

  | Var(name: string)
  | Add(e1: Expr, e2: Expr)

predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}

function optimize(e: Expr): Expr
{
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e2);
    if e1_opt == Const(0) then e2_opt
    else if e2_opt == Const(0) then e1_opt
    else Add(e1_opt, e2_opt)
  case _ => e
}

lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
{
  // Base case: if e is not an addition, then it is already optimized.
  if e != Add(_, _) {
    assert e == optimize(e);
    assert optimal(e);
  } else {
    // Recursive case: optimize the sub-expressions and then match on the optimized sub-expressions.
    var e1_opt := optimize(e.e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e.e2);

   |
36 |     var e2_opt := optimize(e.e2);
   |                                  ^

ex.dfy(36,33): Error: rbrace expected
1 parse errors detected in ex.dfy

  | Var(name: string)

    else if e2_opt == Const(0) then e1_opt

    assert optimal(e);

```dafny
datatype Expr =
  | Const(i: int)
  | Var(name: string)
  | Add(e1: Expr, e2: Expr)

predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}

function optimize(e: Expr): Expr
{
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e2);
    if e1_opt == Const(0) then e2_opt
    else if e2_opt == Const(0) then e1_opt
    else Add(e1_opt, e2_opt)
  case _ => e
}

lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
{
  // Base case: If e is not an addition, then e is in its simplest form.
  if e != Add(_, _) {
    // Since e is not an addition, it must be a constant, a variable, or a non-optimized addition.
    // In any case, it is optimal.
  }
  // Inductive case: e is an addition.
  else {
    // Optimize the sub-expressions of e.
    var e1_opt := optimize(e.e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e.e2);

    // Recursively apply the lemma to the optimized sub-expressions.
    OptimizerOptimal(e1_opt);
    OptimizerOptimal(e2_opt);

    // The optimized expression is optimal.

```dafny
datatype Expr =
  | Const(i: int)
  | Var(name: string)
  | Add(e1: Expr, e2: Expr)

predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}

function optimize(e: Expr): Expr
{
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e2);
    if e1_opt == Const(0) then e2_opt
    else if e2_opt == Const(0) then e1_opt
    else Add(e1_opt, e2_opt)
  case _ => e
}

lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
{
  // Proof by structural induction on the shape of e.
  // The base case is when e is a constant or a variable,
  // in which case the optimized expression is the same as e,
  // and so it is clearly optimal.

  // The optimized expression is either the optimized first subexpression,
  // the optimized second subexpression,
  // or a new addition expression with the optimized subexpressions.
  // In each case, we recursively invoke the lemma on the subexpressions,
  // and since the subexpressions are optimal,
  // it follows that the optimized expression is also optimal.
}

```dafny
datatype Expr =
  | Const(i: int)
  | Var(name: string)
  | Add(e1: Expr, e2: Expr)

predicate optimal(e: Expr) {
  match e
  case Add(Const(0), _) => false
  case Add(_, Const(0)) => false
  case Add(e1, e2) => optimal(e1) && optimal(e2)
  case _ => true
}

function optimize(e: Expr): Expr
{
  match e
  case Add(e1, e2) =>
    var e1_opt := optimize(e1);
    var e2_opt := optimize(e2);
    if e1_opt == Const(0) then e2_opt
    else if e2_opt == Const(0) then e1_opt
    else Add(e1_opt, e2_opt)
  case _ => e
}

lemma OptimizerOptimal(e: Expr)
  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
{
  // Proof by structural induction on the shape of e.
  // The base case is when e is a constant or a variable,
  // in which case the optimized expression is the same as e,
  // and so it is clearly optimal.

  // The inductive case is when e is an addition.
  // The optimized expression is either the optimized first subexpression,
  // the optimized second subexpression,
  // or a new addition expression with the optimized subexpressions.
  // In each case, we recursively invoke the lemma on the subexpressions,
  // and since the subexpressions are optimal,
  // it follows that the optimized expression is also optimal.
}
```

  | Var(name: string)

  ensures optimal(optimize(e))
